//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Bundesarchiv_Bild_199-1992-089-19Acropped.jpg/340px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_199-1992-089-19Acropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="402" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_199-1992-089-19Acropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Philip and Elizabeth, <span class="nowrap">October 1992</span></div></div></div>\n<p>In a speech on 24 November 1992, to mark the <a href="/wiki/Ruby_jubilee" title="Ruby jubilee">40th anniversary</a> of her accession, Elizabeth called 1992 her <i><a href="/wiki/Annus_horribilis" title="Annus horribilis">annus horribilis</a></i>, meaning <i>horrible year</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Republican feeling in Britain had risen because of press estimates of the Queen\'s private wealth \xe2\x80\x93 which were contradicted by the Palace \xe2\x80\x93 and reports of affairs and strained marriages among her extended family.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In March, her second son, Prince Andrew, and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Sarah,_Duchess_of_York" title="Sarah, Duchess of York">Sarah</a>, separated; in April, her daughter, Princess Anne, divorced Captain <a href="/wiki/Mark_Phillips" title="Mark Phillips">Mark Phillips</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> during a state visit to Germany in October, angry demonstrators in <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a> threw eggs at her;<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> and, in November, <a href="/wiki/1992_Windsor_Castle_fire" title="1992 Windsor Castle fire">a large fire</a> broke out at Windsor Castle, one of her official residences. The monarchy came under increased criticism and public scrutiny.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In an unusually personal speech, the Queen said that any institution must expect criticism, but suggested it be done with "a touch of humour, gentleness and understanding".<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">John Major</a>, announced reforms to the royal finances planned since the previous year, including the Queen paying <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> from 1993 onwards, and a reduction in the <a href="/wiki/Civil_list" title="Civil list">civil list</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In December, Prince Charles and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana</a>, formally separated.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The year ended with a lawsuit as the Queen sued <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> newspaper for breach of copyright when it published the text of her <a href="/wiki/Royal_Christmas_Message" title="Royal Christmas Message">annual Christmas message</a> two days before it was broadcast. The newspaper was forced to pay her legal fees and donated \xc2\xa3200,000 to charity.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the years to follow, public revelations on the state of Charles and Diana\'s marriage continued.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Even though support for republicanism in Britain seemed higher than at any time in living memory, republicanism was still a minority viewpoint, and the Queen herself had high approval ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Criticism was focused on the institution of the monarchy itself and the Queen\'s wider family rather than her own behaviour and actions.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In consultation with her husband and the Prime Minister, John Major, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Carey" title="George Carey">George Carey</a>, and her private secretary, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fellowes,_Baron_Fellowes" title="Robert Fellowes, Baron Fellowes">Robert Fellowes</a>, she wrote to Charles and Diana at the end of December 1995, saying a divorce was desirable.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 1997, a year after the divorce, Diana was killed in <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Death of Diana, Princess of Wales">a car crash in Paris</a>. The Queen was on holiday with her extended family at <a href="/wiki/Balmoral_Castle" title="Balmoral Castle">Balmoral</a>. Diana\'s two sons by Charles \xe2\x80\x93 Princes <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">William</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Harry" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Harry">Harry</a> \xe2\x80\x93 wanted to attend church and so the Queen and Prince Philip took them that morning.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> After that single public appearance, for five days the Queen and the Duke shielded their grandsons from the intense press interest by keeping them at Balmoral where they could grieve in private,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> but the royal family\'s seclusion and the failure to fly a flag at <a href="/wiki/Half-mast" title="Half-mast">half-mast</a> over Buckingham Palace caused public dismay.<sup id="cite_ref-MacQueen_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacQueen-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Pressured by the hostile reaction, the Queen agreed to return to London and do a live television broadcast on 5 September, the day before <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana\'s funeral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In the broadcast, she expressed admiration for Diana and her feelings "as a grandmother" for the two princes.<sup id="cite_ref-b&amp;b_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b&amp;b-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> As a result, much of the public hostility evaporated.<sup id="cite_ref-b&amp;b_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b&amp;b-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 1997, the Queen and her husband held a reception at <a href="/wiki/Banqueting_House,_Whitehall" title="Banqueting House, Whitehall">Banqueting House</a> to mark their golden wedding anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-G-Wedding-Anniversary_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G-Wedding-Anniversary-149">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> She made a speech and praised Philip for his role as a consort, referring to him as "my strength and stay".<sup id="cite_ref-G-Wedding-Anniversary_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G-Wedding-Anniversary-149">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_II_greets_NASA_GSFC_employees,_May_8,_2007_edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Elizabeth_II_greets_NASA_GSFC_employees%2C_May_8%2C_2007_edit.jpg/170px-Elizabeth_II_greets_NASA_GSFC_employees%2C_May_8%2C_2007_edit.jpg" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Elizabeth_II_greets_NASA_GSFC_employees%2C_May_8%2C_2007_edit.jpg/255px-Elizabeth_II_greets_NASA_GSFC_employees%2C_May_8%2C_2007_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Elizabeth_II_greets_NASA_GSFC_employees%2C_May_8%2C_2007_edit.jpg/340px-Elizabeth_II_greets_NASA_GSFC_employees%2C_May_8%2C_2007_edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1488" data-file-height="2060" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_II_greets_NASA_GSFC_employees,_May_8,_2007_edit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Elizabeth in 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2002, Elizabeth marked her <a href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Golden Jubilee of Elizabeth II">Golden Jubilee</a>. Her sister and mother died in February and March respectively, and the media speculated whether the Jubilee would be a success or a failure.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> She again undertook an extensive tour of her realms, which began in Jamaica in February, where she called the farewell banquet "memorable" after a power cut plunged the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_House,_Jamaica" title="King&#39;s House, Jamaica">King\'s House</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Official_residence" title="Official residence">official residence</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Jamaica" title="Governor-General of Jamaica">governor-general</a>, into darkness.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> As in 1977, there were street parties and commemorative events, and monuments were named to honour the occasion. A million people attended each day of the three-day main Jubilee celebration in London,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and the enthusiasm shown by the public for the Queen was greater than many journalists had expected.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Though generally healthy throughout her life, in 2003 she had <a href="/wiki/Laparoscopic_surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Laparoscopic surgery">keyhole surgery</a> on both knees. In October 2006, she missed the opening of the new <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Stadium" title="Emirates Stadium">Emirates Stadium</a> because of a strained back muscle that had been troubling her since the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>, citing unnamed sources, reported the Queen was "exasperated and frustrated" by the policies of the British Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, that she was concerned the <a href="/wiki/British_Armed_Forces" title="British Armed Forces">British Armed Forces</a> were overstretched in Iraq and Afghanistan, and that she had raised concerns over rural and countryside issues with Blair.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> She was, however, said to admire Blair\'s efforts to achieve peace in Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> She became the first British monarch to celebrate a diamond wedding anniversary in November 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> On 20 March 2008, at the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a> <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_Cathedral,_Armagh_(Church_of_Ireland)" title="St Patrick&#39;s Cathedral, Armagh (Church of Ireland)">St Patrick\'s Cathedral, Armagh</a>, the Queen attended the first <a href="/wiki/Royal_Maundy" title="Royal Maundy">Maundy service</a> held outside England and Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span></h3>\n<p>The Queen addressed the United Nations for a second time in 2010, again in her capacity as Queen of all Commonwealth realms and Head of the Commonwealth.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-159">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The UN Secretary General, <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>, introduced her as "an anchor for our age".<sup id="cite_ref-BBCUN_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCUN-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> During her visit to New York, which followed a tour of Canada, she officially opened a memorial garden for British victims of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCUN_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCUN-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> The Queen\'s visit to Australia in October 2011 \xe2\x80\x93 her sixteenth visit since 1954 \xe2\x80\x93 was called her "farewell tour" in the press because of her age.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> By invitation of the Irish President, <a href="/wiki/Mary_McAleese" title="Mary McAleese">Mary McAleese</a>, the Queen made the first <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II%27s_state_visit_to_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II&#39;s state visit to the Republic of Ireland">state visit to the Republic of Ireland</a> by a British monarch in May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Day_194_-_West_Midlands_Police_-_Royal_Diamond_Jubilee_Visit_(7555521830).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Day_194_-_West_Midlands_Police_-_Royal_Diamond_Jubilee_Visit_%287555521830%29.jpg/220px-Day_194_-_West_Midlands_Police_-_Royal_Diamond_Jubilee_Visit_%287555521830%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Day_194_-_West_Midlands_Police_-_Royal_Diamond_Jubilee_Visit_%287555521830%29.jpg/330px-Day_194_-_West_Midlands_Police_-_Royal_Diamond_Jubilee_Visit_%287555521830%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Day_194_-_West_Midlands_Police_-_Royal_Diamond_Jubilee_Visit_%287555521830%29.jpg/440px-Day_194_-_West_Midlands_Police_-_Royal_Diamond_Jubilee_Visit_%287555521830%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Day_194_-_West_Midlands_Police_-_Royal_Diamond_Jubilee_Visit_(7555521830).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Elizabeth visiting <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> in <span class="nowrap">July 2012</span> as part of her Diamond Jubilee tour</div></div></div><p>\nElizabeth\'s <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Diamond Jubilee of Elizabeth II">Diamond Jubilee</a> in 2012 marked 60 years on the throne, and celebrations were held throughout her realms, the wider Commonwealth, and beyond. In a message released on <a href="/wiki/Accession_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession Day">Accession Day</a>, Elizabeth wrote:</p><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In this special year, as I dedicate myself anew to your service, I hope we will all be reminded of the power of togetherness and the convening strength of family, friendship and good neighbourliness&#160;... I hope also that this Jubilee year will be a time to give thanks for the great advances that have been made since 1952 and to look forward to the future with clear head and warm heart.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>She and her husband undertook an extensive tour of the United Kingdom, while her children and grandchildren embarked on royal tours of other Commonwealth states on her behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> On 4 June, Jubilee beacons were lit around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In November, the Queen and her husband celebrated their sapphire wedding anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> On 18 December, she became the first British sovereign to attend a peacetime <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet meeting</a> since <a href="/wiki/George_III" class="mw-redirect" title="George III">George III</a> in 1781.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Queen, who opened the <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">1976 Summer Olympics</a> in Montreal, also opened the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Paralympics" title="2012 Summer Paralympics">Paralympics</a> in London, making her the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_who_have_opened_the_Olympic_Games" title="List of people who have opened the Olympic Games">head of state to open</a> two Olympic Games in two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> For the London Olympics, she played herself in <a href="/wiki/Happy_%26_Glorious" class="mw-redirect" title="Happy &amp; Glorious">a short film</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Craig" title="Daniel Craig">Daniel Craig</a> as <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> On 4 April 2013, she received an honorary <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA</a> for her patronage of the film industry and was called "the most memorable <a href="/wiki/Bond_girl" title="Bond girl">Bond girl</a> yet" at the award ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 March 2013, Elizabeth was admitted to <a href="/wiki/King_Edward_VII%27s_Hospital" title="King Edward VII&#39;s Hospital">King Edward VII\'s Hospital</a> as a precaution after developing symptoms of <a href="/wiki/Gastroenteritis" title="Gastroenteritis">gastroenteritis</a>. She returned to Buckingham Palace the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> A week later, she signed the new <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Charter of the Commonwealth">Commonwealth charter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Because of her age and the need for her to limit travelling, in 2013 she chose not to attend the biennial <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Heads_of_Government_Meeting" title="Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting">meeting of Commonwealth heads of government</a> for the first time in 40 years. She was represented at the summit in Sri Lanka by her son, Prince Charles.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> She had cataract surgery in May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Queen surpassed her great-great-grandmother, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>, to become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_monarchs_by_longevity" title="List of British monarchs by longevity">longest-lived British monarch</a> on 21 December 2007, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_in_Britain_by_length_of_reign#Overall" title="List of monarchs in Britain by length of reign">longest-reigning British monarch</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_longest-reigning_monarchs" title="List of longest-reigning monarchs">longest-reigning queen regnant</a> and female head of state in the world on 9 September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> She is also the "longest-reigning sovereign in Canada\'s modern era".<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">King Louis XIV</a> of France reigned over <a href="/wiki/Canada_(New_France)" title="Canada (New France)">Canada (New France)</a> for longer than Elizabeth.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>) She became the oldest current monarch after <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Abdullah of Saudi Arabia">King Abdullah of Saudi Arabia</a> died on 23 January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> She later became the longest-reigning current monarch and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_state_leaders_by_date_of_assumption_of_office" title="List of current state leaders by date of assumption of office">longest-serving current head of state</a> following the death of <a href="/wiki/Bhumibol_Adulyadej" title="Bhumibol Adulyadej">King Bhumibol</a> of Thailand on 13 October 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_state_leaders_by_age" title="Lists of state leaders by age">oldest current head of state</a> on the resignation of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a> on 21 November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> On 6 February 2017, she became the first British monarch to commemorate a <a href="/wiki/Sapphire_Jubilee_of_Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Sapphire Jubilee of Queen Elizabeth II">Sapphire Jubilee</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> and on 20 November, she was the first British monarch to celebrate a platinum wedding anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Prince Philip had retired from his official duties as the Queen\'s consort in August.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Queen does not intend to <a href="/wiki/Abdicate" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdicate">abdicate</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> though Prince Charles is expected to take on more of her duties as Elizabeth, who celebrated her 92nd birthday in 2018, carries out fewer public engagements.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> On 20 April 2018, the government leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> announced that she will be succeeded by Prince Charles as head of the Commonwealth. The Queen stated it was her "sincere wish" that the Prince of Wales would follow her in the role.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Operation_London_Bridge" title="Operation London Bridge">Plans for her death and funeral</a> have been extensively prepared by most British government and media organisations for decades.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_perception_and_character">Public perception and character</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Personality_and_image_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Personality and image of Elizabeth II">Personality and image of Elizabeth II</a></div>\n<p>Since Elizabeth rarely gives interviews, little is known of her personal feelings. As a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarch</a>, she has not expressed her own political opinions in a public forum. She does have a deep sense of religious and civic duty, and takes her coronation oath seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Aside from her <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom#Religious_role" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">official religious role</a> as <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Governor_of_the_Church_of_England" title="Supreme Governor of the Church of England">Supreme Governor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">established</a> <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>, she is a member of that church and also of the national <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> She has demonstrated support for <a href="/wiki/Interfaith_dialogue" title="Interfaith dialogue">inter-faith</a> relations and has met with leaders of other churches and religions, including five popes: <a href="/wiki/Pius_XII" class="mw-redirect" title="Pius XII">Pius XII</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_XXIII" class="mw-redirect" title="John XXIII">John XXIII</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_II" class="mw-redirect" title="John Paul II">John Paul II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benedict_XVI" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Francis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> A personal note about her faith often features in her annual <a href="/wiki/Royal_Christmas_Message" title="Royal Christmas Message">Christmas message</a> broadcast to the Commonwealth. In 2000, she said:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>To many of us, our beliefs are of fundamental importance. For me the teachings of Christ and my own personal accountability before God provide a framework in which I try to lead my life. I, like so many of you, have drawn great comfort in difficult times from Christ\'s words and example.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Reagan_and_Queen_Elizabeth_II_1982.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Elizabeth and Ronald Reagan on black horses. He bare-headed; she in a headscarf; both in tweeds, jodhpurs and riding boots." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/President_Reagan_and_Queen_Elizabeth_II_1982.jpg/220px-President_Reagan_and_Queen_Elizabeth_II_1982.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/President_Reagan_and_Queen_Elizabeth_II_1982.jpg/330px-President_Reagan_and_Queen_Elizabeth_II_1982.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/President_Reagan_and_Queen_Elizabeth_II_1982.jpg/440px-President_Reagan_and_Queen_Elizabeth_II_1982.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="503" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Reagan_and_Queen_Elizabeth_II_1982.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Elizabeth and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> riding at Windsor, <span class="nowrap">June 1982</span></div></div></div>\n<p>She is <a href="/wiki/Patronage" title="Patronage">patron</a> of over 600 organisations and charities.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Her main leisure interests include <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrianism</a> and dogs, especially her <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Welsh_Corgi" title="Pembroke Welsh Corgi">Pembroke Welsh Corgis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Her lifelong <a href="/wiki/Royal_corgis" title="Royal corgis">love of corgis</a> began in 1933 with Dookie, the first corgi owned by her family.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Scenes of a relaxed, informal home life have occasionally been witnessed; she and her family, from time to time, prepare a meal together and do the washing up afterwards.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1950s, as a young woman at the start of her reign, Elizabeth was depicted as a glamorous "fairytale Queen".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> After the trauma of the Second World War, it was a time of hope, a period of progress and achievement heralding a "new Elizabethan age".<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Grigg,_2nd_Baron_Altrincham" title="John Grigg, 2nd Baron Altrincham">Lord Altrincham</a>\'s accusation in 1957 that her speeches sounded like those of a "priggish schoolgirl" was an extremely rare criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1960s, attempts to portray a more modern image of the monarchy were made in the television documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Royal_Family_(documentary)" title="Royal Family (documentary)">Royal Family</a></i> and by televising Prince Charles\'s <a href="/wiki/Investiture_of_the_Prince_of_Wales" title="Investiture of the Prince of Wales">investiture as Prince of Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> In public, she took to wearing mostly solid-colour overcoats and decorative hats, which allow her to be seen easily in a crowd.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At her <a href="/wiki/Silver_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Silver Jubilee of Elizabeth II">Silver Jubilee</a> in 1977, the crowds and celebrations were genuinely enthusiastic,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> but in the 1980s, public criticism of the royal family increased, as the personal and working lives of Elizabeth\'s children came under media scrutiny.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Elizabeth\'s popularity sank to a low point in the 1990s. Under pressure from public opinion, she began to pay income tax for the first time, and Buckingham Palace was opened to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Discontent with the monarchy reached its peak on the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Death of Diana, Princess of Wales">death of Diana, Princess of Wales</a>, though Elizabeth\'s personal popularity and support for the monarchy rebounded after her live television broadcast to the world five days after Diana\'s death.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 1999, a <a href="/wiki/Australian_republic_referendum,_1999" title="Australian republic referendum, 1999">referendum in Australia</a> on the future of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Australia" title="Monarchy of Australia">Australian monarchy</a> favoured its retention in preference to an indirectly elected head of state.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Polls in Britain in 2006 and 2007 revealed strong support for Elizabeth,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> and in 2012, her Diamond Jubilee year, approval ratings hit 90 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Referendums in <a href="/wiki/Tuvaluan_constitutional_referendum,_2008" title="Tuvaluan constitutional referendum, 2008">Tuvalu in 2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vincentian_constitutional_referendum,_2009" title="Vincentian constitutional referendum, 2009">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines in 2009</a> both rejected proposals to become republics.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Elizabeth has been portrayed in a variety of media by many notable artists, including painters <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Annigoni" title="Pietro Annigoni">Pietro Annigoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Blake_(artist)" title="Peter Blake (artist)">Peter Blake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinwe_Chukwuogo-Roy" title="Chinwe Chukwuogo-Roy">Chinwe Chukwuogo-Roy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terence_Cuneo" title="Terence Cuneo">Terence Cuneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucian_Freud" title="Lucian Freud">Lucian Freud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rolf_Harris" title="Rolf Harris">Rolf Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damien_Hirst" title="Damien Hirst">Damien Hirst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juliet_Pannett" title="Juliet Pannett">Juliet Pannett</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tai-Shan_Schierenberg" title="Tai-Shan Schierenberg">Tai-Shan Schierenberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NPG1_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPG1-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Notable photographers of Elizabeth have included <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Beaton" title="Cecil Beaton">Cecil Beaton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yousuf_Karsh" title="Yousuf Karsh">Yousuf Karsh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annie_Leibovitz" title="Annie Leibovitz">Annie Leibovitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Anson,_5th_Earl_of_Lichfield" title="Patrick Anson, 5th Earl of Lichfield">Lord Lichfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terry_O%27Neill_(photographer)" title="Terry O&#39;Neill (photographer)">Terry O\'Neill</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Swannell_(photographer)" title="John Swannell (photographer)">John Swannell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Wilding" title="Dorothy Wilding">Dorothy Wilding</a>. The first official portrait of Elizabeth was taken by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Adams_(photographer)" title="Marcus Adams (photographer)">Marcus Adams</a> in 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-NPG_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPG-218">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Finances_of_the_British_royal_family" title="Finances of the British royal family">Finances of the British royal family</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Paradise_Papers" title="Paradise Papers">Paradise Papers</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandringham_House_garden.jpg" class="image"><img alt="View of Sandingham House from the south bank of the Upper Lake" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sandringham_House_garden.jpg/220px-Sandringham_House_garden.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sandringham_House_garden.jpg/330px-Sandringham_House_garden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sandringham_House_garden.jpg/440px-Sandringham_House_garden.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1146" data-file-height="722" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandringham_House_garden.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sandringham_House" title="Sandringham House">Sandringham House</a>, Elizabeth\'s private residence in <a href="/wiki/Sandringham,_Norfolk" title="Sandringham, Norfolk">Norfolk</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Elizabeth\'s personal fortune has been the subject of speculation for many years. In 1971 <a href="/wiki/Jock_Colville" title="Jock Colville">Jock Colville</a>, her former private secretary and a director of her bank, <a href="/wiki/Coutts" title="Coutts">Coutts</a>, estimated her wealth at \xc2\xa32&#160;million (equivalent to about \xc2\xa326&#160;million in 2016<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-219">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> In 1993, Buckingham Palace called estimates of \xc2\xa3100&#160;million "grossly overstated".<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> In 2002, she inherited an estate worth an estimated \xc2\xa370&#160;million from her mother.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List_2017" title="Sunday Times Rich List 2017">Sunday Times Rich List 2017</a></i> estimated her personal wealth at \xc2\xa3360&#160;million, making her the 329th richest person in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-richlist2017_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richlist2017-224">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Collection" title="Royal Collection">Royal Collection</a>, which includes thousands of historic works of art and the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Jewels_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Crown Jewels of the United Kingdom">Crown Jewels</a>, is not owned by the Queen personally but is held <a href="/wiki/Trust_law" title="Trust law">in trust</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> as are her official residences, such as <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-res_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-res-226">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Lancaster" title="Duchy of Lancaster">Duchy of Lancaster</a>, a property portfolio valued at \xc2\xa3472&#160;million in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sandringham_House" title="Sandringham House">Sandringham House</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balmoral_Castle" title="Balmoral Castle">Balmoral Castle</a> are personally owned by the Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-res_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-res-226">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> The British <a href="/wiki/Crown_Estate" title="Crown Estate">Crown Estate</a> \xe2\x80\x93 with holdings of \xc2\xa312&#160;billion in 2016<sup id="cite_ref-richlist2017_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richlist2017-224">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 is held in trust and cannot be sold or owned by Elizabeth in a personal capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Titles.2C_styles.2C_honours.2C_and_arms"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles,_styles,_honours,_and_arms">Titles, styles, honours, and arms</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_and_styles">Titles and styles</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_titles_and_honours_of_Elizabeth_II" title="List of titles and honours of Elizabeth II">List of titles and honours of Elizabeth II</a></div>\n<ul><li>21 April 1926&#160;&#8211;&#32;11 December 1936: Her Royal Highness Princess Elizabeth of York</li>\n<li>11 December 1936&#160;&#8211;&#32;20 November 1947: Her Royal Highness The Princess Elizabeth</li>\n<li>20 November 1947&#160;&#8211;&#32;6 February 1952: Her Royal Highness The Princess Elizabeth, Duchess of Edinburgh</li>\n<li>Since 6 February 1952: Her Majesty The Queen</li></ul>\n<p>Elizabeth has held many titles and honorary military positions throughout the Commonwealth, is Sovereign of many orders in her own countries, and has received honours and awards from around the world. In each of her realms she has a distinct title that follows a similar formula: <i>Queen of Jamaica and her other realms and territories</i> in Jamaica, <i>Queen of Australia and her other realms and territories</i> in Australia, etc. In the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, which are <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a> rather than separate realms, she is known as <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Normandy" title="Duke of Normandy">Duke of Normandy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_Mann" title="Lord of Mann">Lord of Mann</a>, respectively. Additional styles include <a href="/wiki/Fidei_defensor" class="mw-redirect" title="Fidei defensor">Defender of the Faith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Lancaster" title="Duke of Lancaster">Duke of Lancaster</a>. When in conversation with the Queen, the practice is to initially address her as <i>Your Majesty</i> and thereafter as <i>Ma\'am</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms">Arms</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Flags_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Flags of Elizabeth II">Flags of Elizabeth II</a></div>\n<p>From 21 April 1944 until her accession, Elizabeth\'s arms consisted of a <a href="/wiki/Lozenge_(heraldry)" title="Lozenge (heraldry)">lozenge</a> bearing the <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom</a> differenced with a <a href="/wiki/Label_(heraldry)" title="Label (heraldry)">label</a> of three points <a href="/wiki/Argent" title="Argent">argent</a>, the centre point bearing a <a href="/wiki/Tudor_rose" title="Tudor rose">Tudor rose</a> and the first and third a <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Cross">cross of St George</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Upon her accession, she inherited the various arms her father held as sovereign. The Queen also possesses <a href="/wiki/Banner#Heraldic_banners" title="Banner">royal standards</a> and personal flags for use in <a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal Standard of the United Kingdom">the United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_standards_of_Canada" title="Royal standards of Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Personal_Australian_Flag" title="Queen&#39;s Personal Australian Flag">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Personal_Flag_for_New_Zealand" title="Queen&#39;s Personal Flag for New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Personal_Jamaican_Flag" title="Queen&#39;s Personal Jamaican Flag">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Personal_Barbadian_Flag" title="Queen&#39;s Personal Barbadian Flag">Barbados</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Personal_Flag_of_Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Personal Flag of Queen Elizabeth II">elsewhere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="overflow:auto;">\n<table border="0" style="margin:auto; width:100%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="20%"><div class="center"><div href="/wiki/List_of_things_named_after_Elizabeth_II" title="List of things named after Elizabeth II">List of things named after Elizabeth II</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-birthday-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-birthday_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Official_Birthday" title="Queen&#39;s Official Birthday">Queen\'s Official Birthday</a> for an explanation of why Elizabeth II\'s official birthdays are not on the same day as her actual one.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-baptism-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-baptism_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Her godparents were: King George V and Queen Mary; Lord Strathmore; <a href="/wiki/Prince_Arthur,_Duke_of_Connaught_and_Strathearn" title="Prince Arthur, Duke of Connaught and Strathearn">Prince Arthur, Duke of Connaught and Strathearn</a> (her paternal great-granduncle); <a href="/wiki/Princess_Mary,_Viscountess_Lascelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Princess Mary, Viscountess Lascelles">Princess Mary, Viscountess Lascelles</a> (her paternal aunt); and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Elphinstone,_Lady_Elphinstone" title="Mary Elphinstone, Lady Elphinstone">Lady Elphinstone</a> (her maternal aunt).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-television-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-television_73-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Television coverage of the coronation was instrumental in boosting the medium\'s popularity; the number of <a href="/wiki/Television_licensing_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Television licensing in the United Kingdom">television licences in the United Kingdom</a> doubled to 3&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and many of the more than 20&#160;million British viewers watched television for the first time in the homes of their friends or neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In North America, just under 100 million viewers watched recorded broadcasts.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-arms-233"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-arms_233-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Canada has used three versions of the arms during her reign. This version was used between 1957 and 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; id="The_generations_indicate_descent_from_George_I,_who_formalised_the_use_of_the_titles_prince_and_princess_for_members_of_the_British_royal_family._Where_a_princess_may_have_been_or_is_descended_from_George_I_more_than_once,_her_most_senior_descent,_by_which_she_bore_or_bears_her_title,_is_used.">The generations indicate descent from <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Great_Britain" title="George I of Great Britain">George I</a>, who formalised the use of the titles <i>prince</i> and <i>princess</i> for members of the British royal family. Where a princess may have been or is descended from George I more than once, her most senior descent, by which she bore or bears her title, is used.</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"
